# [Rules][1]

**Ruff supports over 800 lint rules**, many of which are inspired by popular tools like Flake8,
isort, pyupgrade, and others. Regardless of the rule's origin, Ruff re-implements every rule in Rust
as a first-party feature.

By default, Ruff enables Flake8's `F` rules, along with a subset of the `E` rules, omitting any
stylistic rules that overlap with the use of a formatter, like `ruff format` or [Black][2].

If you're just getting started with Ruff, **the default rule set is a great place to start**: it
catches a wide variety of common errors (like unused imports) with zero configuration.

## [Legend][3]

ğŸ§ª The rule is unstable and is in ["preview"][4].
âš ï¸ The rule has been deprecated and will be removed in a future release.
âŒ The rule has been removed only the documentation is available.
ğŸ› ï¸ The rule is automatically fixable by the `--fix` command-line option.

All rules not marked as preview, deprecated or removed are stable.
